The Audit Office Abolishes Malpractices in Salt Affairs 170

A Circular is Issued to All Bureaus and Offices for Compliance

Since the General Audit Office of Salt Affairs of the Ministry of Finance received the order from the Ministry to take over various administrative organs of salt affairs, it has been making great efforts in the work of reorganization. In addition to greatly reducing the original administrative personnel, it has recently begun to clear up the long-standing malpractices of salt affairs. It is said that the biggest of the administrative malpractices is the acceptance of malpractices. The General Office has issued a circular to all subordinates, instructing them to investigate and eliminate all the original malpractices in their respective districts. In the future, no officials under their jurisdiction may accept malpractices or other gifts. If they dare to violate this, they will be severely punished upon discovery. On one hand, the主管机关 (responsible authorities) of each subordinate department should announce to merchants and people that they should not offer malpractices to salt affairs personnel in the future. If they are found, they will be prosecuted for bribery. If there is any extortion under the pretext of needing money, they are also allowed to report it for investigation. The General Office's intention to actively reorganize salt affairs administration can be seen in general. It is heard that the circular has been issued to the four branches of the Eastern Huai, Northern Huai, Yangzhou, Songjiang, Liangzhe, and Fujian Provinces, as well as the four-shore audit offices and the Henan tax collection bureau. The full text of the circular is recorded below for compliance.

Page 14

It is an order for compliance. It has been found that the administrative affairs of salt affairs in the district

have already been taken over by the局 (Bureau) (所) (Office) (处) according to the order of the Ministry, and all the previous bad habits are extremely difficult to carry out. 净清 (clean up) and do not let the 진행 (progress) of the textile整理 (reorganization) work. It has been made known that they have complied. However, after investigation, the biggest problem in the administrative aspects of salt affairs is the acceptance of malpractices. It has been practiced for a long time, and it has been taken for granted. The giver considers it an obligation, and the receiver also regards it as a right to be enjoyed. In reality, it is no different from accepting bribes and seeking personal gain. If we want to achieve the clarity of salt affairs administration, we must make the elimination of malpractices an urgent task. All the original malpractices in the salt affairs aspects of the district must be thoroughly investigated and eliminated. In addition, officials under their jurisdiction should be strictly ordered that no one should accept malpractices or other gifts from merchants and people in the future. If they dare to do so, they will be severely punished upon discovery. On one hand, it is still necessary to announce to the merchants and people that they are not allowed to offer any malpractices or gifts to salt affairs personnel in the future. If there are those who cling to old habits and do not know how to reform, they will be prosecuted for bribery and punished in the same way as the receiver. If there is any case of salt affairs personnel asking for money under the pretext of wanting money, they are also allowed to report it based on the circumstances for investigation. We will keep the reporters of merchants secret and will not cause any delay. Officials and merchants will work together to ensure that the long-term malpractices will be completely eradicated in the shortest possible time. From now on, the malpractice will be eradicated and the atmosphere will be clean, which will be in line with the Ministry's intention to actively reorganize. In addition to issuing orders for compliance, it is urgently ordered that the局 (Bureau) (所) (Office) (处) comply strictly and not be negligent. The compliance situation should be reported for verification. This order.

Interpretation of Foreigners Obtaining Patent Rights in China 174

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Replied to Lawyer Xu Shihui

The Nature of Reciprocal Benefits for Sino-Foreign

Not Applicable to Countries That Have Not Reciprocated

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a reply to lawyer Xu Shihui, explaining the measures for foreigners to obtain patent rights in China, stating, "We received your letter on the 6th of this month, inquiring about whether the industrial manufacturing patent rights obtained by foreigners in foreign countries can be effective within China. If they cannot be effective within China, can they apply for registration of their patent rights with the Ministry of Industry in order to protect their rights? After investigation, Section 10 of the Sino-American Supplementary Treaty on Commerce and Navigation of the 29th Year of Guangxu states, "The United States government allows Chinese people to register their inventions in the United States and issue invention licenses to protect their rights to self-management and self-use. The Chinese government also agrees to establish a special management office for inventions in the future. After the establishment of the special management office and the enactment of special laws on inventions, any inventions in China that are eligible for approval and have already been licensed by the United States, if they do not violate the inventions of Chinese people, can be protected by issuing special licenses to American people after paying the regulations fees. Later, the second half of Section 15 of the Sino-Portuguese Supplementary Treaty of the 30th Year of Guangxu also has the same provision. That is to say, if the people of these two countries want to maintain their patent rights in China, they should apply to the Ministry of Industry for approval and registration in accordance with the treaty before they can enjoy them. However, it should be noted that this is a special clause specially stipulated for the mutual protection of patent rights between the two countries, which is a matter of reciprocity. It is different from the unconditional most-favored-nation treatment mentioned in other clauses. Therefore, this benefit cannot be extrapolated to other countries that have not signed reciprocal special clauses. The opinions of several associations are as such. If the lawyer does not mind seeking details, he can inquire with the Ministry of Industry in order to strike a fair balance.

Reply Letter of the Taxpayers' Association on the Water Issue 175

Recognizes That the Municipal Council's Reply Letter Does Not Attach Importance to the Case

Discuss Further Reasonable and Practical Methods

The Shanghai Concession Taxpayers' Chinese Association has previously received letters from various real estate companies and rental agencies, reporting that the water rates have increased sharply after the conversion of water meters and requesting that measures be taken to negotiate. The association has forwarded the letters to the Municipal Council for handling. It was not until September 24 that the association received a reply from the Municipal Council. The association specially sent a letter yesterday to reply to the companies and agencies, stating, "Regarding the case of the sharp increase in water rates calculated by water meters, which cannot be afforded, we have repeatedly sent letters to the 总办 (Chief Executive Officer) of the Shanghai Municipal Council, requesting that measures be taken quickly. It was not until September 24 that we received a reply from the 总办 (Chief Executive Officer), which reads, "We have received your letter of September 19, concerning the low collection of water fees by the Shanghai Water Company. We have found that the various statements issued by this bureau regarding water and water meters have been published in the gazette and should have been reviewed by you. We will not repeat them. As for the cases mentioned in your letter, it is easier to consider the high and low of the fees if we first find out the amount of water used in each case and the amount of water fees per unit. Your association does not seem to pay attention to this when writing the letter. This bureau has reported its position on the issue of water prices from time to time and published it in the gazette. We cannot explain everything in one letter. If your association can send a representative to come, I will explain it, and if there are any accumulated opinions, we can discuss them face-to-face. I hope that your association can take this opportunity to carefully consider the points raised in your letter, and it will be more helpful to avoid making empty threats. This bureau is very concerned about the promotion of the interests of the citizens, and it is especially concerned about practical facts." In addition to recognizing that the case has not been taken seriously, we will discuss further reasonable and practical methods that are easy to implement and do not increase the burden on poor small households. We hereby send this letter for your information and request your valuable opinions to correct our shortcomings.

Yao Wenxuan and Others Oppose Selling Accumulated Grain and Public Property 176

Document Submitted to the Ministry of Interior and Jiangsu Provincial Government

Shanghai citizens Yao Wenxuan, Shen Wenbin, Jia Fengyun, Shi Qiguang, Wang Yugang, Tang Fuqian, Hu Renfeng, Zhang Zongfu, Gu Xiaoqing, Zhu Lijian, Jin Qingzhang, Cao Yuanjun, Li Zuyou, Zheng Yi, Wang Quanyun, Tai Xichu, Huang Yunzhen, Qian Jiao, Liu Donghai, Jia Jiying, Sheng Linshu, and others oppose selling accumulated grain, real estate, and public property, and have submitted documents to the Executive Yuan and other bodies. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, we present the document submitted to the Ministry of Interior and Jiangsu Provincial Government as follows: The document states, "Regarding the matter of handling accumulated grain in Shanghai, there are indeed special circumstances. We request that public property be preserved to appease the people and address famine relief. The Shanghai Municipal and County Division of the Accumulated Grain Property Valuation Committee has already determined the prices and resolved to auction them. The committee is acting on the principle of fairness across the city and county. However, since the prices have already been assessed and there are differences in the size of houses and land, compensation can be made with existing funds. If there is no other intention, why must property be disposed of? Upon investigation, Shanghai's accumulated grain, from the sixth year of Tongzhi to the sixth year of Guangxu, over seven terms of land tax, yielded only 110,700 strings of cash. Over 20,300 stones of grain were purchased for storage, but due to the low and damp terrain, the grain was prone to mold and spoilage. Through years of drying, replacement, and exchanges, there were significant losses. Therefore, in the sixth year of Guangxu, it was decided to accumulate cash instead of grain. A request was submitted to Magistrate Mo Xiangzhi, who received approval from Governor Tan Junpei. During the upheavals of Gengzi and Xinhai, financial panic and market instability occurred. Deeply aware of the dangers of accumulating cash, a portion of the deposits was used in the third year of the Republic to convert empty warehouses into residential buildings, generating rental income and interest. Within ten years, over 100,000 yuan was accumulated, which was entirely borrowed by He Fenglin, the Songhu Military Governor. Our people learned a severe lesson from this, leading to the consensus that accumulating property is better than accumulating cash. This is the experience our people have gained through repeated changes. Recently, your Ministry issued a general order to all counties to replenish granaries, a noble intention and sound policy that should be followed. However, in Shanghai, agricultural production consists of 70% cotton and 30% rice. Residents rely on imported rice for their food. Fortunately, rice merchants converge, and rice from inland and overseas gathers in Shanghai. Farmers are only concerned about lacking money, not about lacking rice. This is Shanghai's unique situation, different from inland areas. The city has a dense population of approximately 3 million, and the county has over 100,000.

The daily rice consumption is 30,000 to 40,000 stones. Even if the current estimated land price is used to purchase rice, it would only yield 50,000 stones, enough for the city and county for only two days, which is still insufficient. To prepare adequately, it would be necessary to raise 10 million yuan and accumulate 1 million stones of rice to feed the people for one month. This is Shanghai's unique situation, different from other counties. As for converting immovable property into movable property to earn interest, it may indeed yield more than rent. However, today, all institutions and organizations are financially strained. Upon seeing this cash, everyone will try to get their hands on it. We fear that there will not only be one He Fenglin, but countless He Fenglins who will use borrowing as a pretext, obtain it by force or cunning, and gradually dissipate it. Even if the government prohibits misappropriation, the people closely supervise, and the officials in charge can overcome personal feelings and refuse to compromise, there is no guarantee against unexpected losses. Furthermore, Shanghai is currently short of cash and flooded with bonds. Speculative ventures are constantly changing. Regardless of the business, there is a possibility of failure. This is also the experience our people have gained, leading them to believe that accumulating property is better than accumulating cash. We, the citizens, believe that the foundation of property accumulated by our people over sixty years is used for annual storage of rent and interest, to alleviate medical expenses, provide small-scale famine relief, and, in times of great famine, attract rice merchants with mortgages of 300,000 to 400,000 yuan to provide a continuous supply, which can widely help and reward farmers. Therefore, we dare to request that your Ministry (Government) consider the situation, instruct Shanghai County to divide the land fairly according to the prices assessed by the committee. If there are differences in quantity that are difficult to divide, they should be compensated with cash. Do not auction off farmland, preserve the original property, and prepare for unexpected needs. Then, your Ministry (Government) will have brought profound and far-reaching benefits to the region. Furthermore, Shanghai rice merchants are willing to donate five cents of silver per stone of rice sold to a granary fund, which is estimated to yield 200,000 to 300,000 yuan per year. If the mayor takes advantage of this situation to achieve the storage of 1 million stones, it is also what we, the citizens, earnestly desire. Apart from submitting copies, we respectfully submit this."

Since Pucheng is strategically important, it cannot be defended by an undisciplined, poorly trained, and poorly equipped Provincial Defense Army. Dispute Over the Collision Between the Yunlong and Yongyuan Ships 178

The Yongyuan Shipyard's Yongyuan ship was transporting goods to Beijing and was damaged by the Heng'an Company's Yunlong ship near Shierxu. It has now returned to Shanghai. Due to the issue of responsibility, the two parties are in dispute. Yongyuan submitted a request to the Maritime Bureau yesterday to send personnel for inspection. The details of the situation are recorded below.

Circumstances of the Collision 179

The Yongyuan ship departed for Nanjing on the 3rd of this month to transport flour to Tanggu. At 5:30 PM, while sailing near Yinjiatou on the Jiangmian River in the vicinity of Shierxu, the Yunlong ship was departing from Shierxu. Before the two ships met, the Yongyuan sounded its horn twice, but the Yunlong did not respond. As the Yongyuan proceeded, the Yunlong suddenly yielded to a German merchant ship, the Juhai, and violently collided with the side of the Yongyuan. Caught off guard, the captain of the Yongyuan quickly put the ship in reverse at full speed, fortunately preventing the collision from reaching the engine room. Otherwise, the Yongyuan would have been broken in two. As a result, the third cabin on the starboard side of the Yongyuan was violently struck by the bow of the Yunlong.

Both Ships Damaged 180

The Yongyuan suffered a large hole approximately one zhang in size where it was struck on the outside of the third cabin on the starboard side. Many items on deck were also damaged. Fortunately, it was above the waterline, and the ship, being empty, did not sink. The Yunlong, being heavily loaded, also suffered damage to its bow due to the excessive force of the collision. After the two ships were damaged, they were unable to sail and each sought ways to return to Shanghai for major repairs.

Issue of Responsibility 181

The Yongyuan Shipyard believes that the collision was due to the Yunlong's navigational error and that it should bear full responsibility for the accident. The Yongyuan was damaged on its side, while the Yunlong was damaged on its bow, proving the cause of the collision. The Heng'an Company argues that the Yunlong was yielding to the German ship, resulting in the collision with the Yongyuan, and that the Yongyuan should bear the responsibility. The two parties disagree, causing a major dispute.

Maritime Bureau Inspection 182

The Yongyuan was originally scheduled to enter the dock for major repairs upon arrival in Shanghai. However, due to the issue of responsibility, it reported the incident to the Maritime Bureau yesterday after the ship arrived, requesting that personnel be sent to the ship for inspection to clarify the responsibility and facilitate claiming compensation from Heng'an. At 3:30 PM yesterday, the ship was towed to Ruirong, and the Maritime Bureau's Technical Section sent specialists to inspect the ship.

It is now known that the Executive Committee of the Municipal Party Department has approved the Chamber of Commerce, with the original text as follows: "Noted. After investigation, the employees in the grocery industry, except for shop assistants who are the users, should join the Industry Association. The clerks and labelers are indeed formal workers and can legally organize a union. When it is formally established, they will be properly separated and retired. Therefore, except for the forcibly registering shop assistants, the Union is ordered to stop the preparation committee. The Cooperative Movement in China 194

It is undeniable that China has been weak and humiliated in recent times. However, reformers either cling to theories and specialize in empty talk, not knowing that most of the chaos stems from foreign economic aggression, leading to the bankruptcy of rural areas and widespread famine. It is indeed not easy to demand that people facing hunger and cold devote their energy to patriotism and resisting violence. Therefore, the current plan to govern the country must focus on the fundamentals, which means stabilizing the lives of the majority and guiding the economic development of the entire population. In other words, it should start with promoting the economic well-being of farmers. After all, we are a country founded on agriculture, and farmers account for more than 80% of the national population. If farmers are secure, bandits will be subdued, and then we can achieve prosperity and strength. However, to assist rural areas, it is necessary to first solve the issues of insufficient arable land, low agricultural output, underdeveloped side businesses, and lack of capital. To solve the above problems with a consistent policy, there is nothing better than promoting cooperation. The cooperative system can stabilize prices and improve living standards when applied to consumers, and it can improve technology, develop finance, eliminate the oppression of middlemen, and eliminate the separation between cities and villages when applied to producers. Its ultimate goal is to link producers and consumers, eradicate the bad habit of profiteering, and develop capital without concentrating it in the hands of a few. This is essential for discussing fundamental issues in China today. The promotion of cooperation in China has been going on for years. The annual meeting will soon be held in Suzhou. Therefore, I am writing this article to briefly describe the process, so that those who are concerned about the foundation of the country can gain some insights.

Since the founding of the Republic of China, scholars have recognized the importance of cooperative enterprises. The first to advocate for it was Xue Xianzhou from Xiangshan, who founded the Common People's Society in 1918, which was the earliest organization in our country to promote cooperation. At that time, the influence was such that a trend was started. However, due to the lack of opportunity, it gradually started and stopped. In 1927, when the National Government was established, members of the Central Committee, Li Shizeng, Chiang Kai-shek, and Chen Guofu, suggested to the Central Government to promote cooperation. At that time, the cooperative movement flourished. Chen Guofu, Wang Shiying, Sun Shoulun, Shou Miancheng, and others organized the Chinese Cooperative Society to research theories, promote movements, guide facilities, and investigate businesses. It was established in Shanghai on December 22, 1928. In the past four years, not only has its own business made great progress, but also the cooperative businesses throughout the country have benefited from the support of the society. At the beginning of its establishment, it edited and published the "Cooperative Weekly" as an attachment to the "Republic Daily" in Shanghai. Although only a few members of the society wrote it, it also attracted the attention of the society. When the society was established, it further edited and published books. However, at that time, there were only 22 members.

At the same time, the society entrusted Chen Zhongming, a member studying in France, to investigate the cooperative businesses in the four countries of England, France, Denmark, and Czechoslovakia. Chen returned to China in the autumn of 1929 and wrote "A Study of European Cooperative Businesses". At that time, the society had already started a monthly magazine, initially managed by Hou Houpei, and later by Wang Shiying. Cheng Jingjun was responsible for news and reports. A series of books have also been published, as many as thirteen kinds. Important books on Chinese and Western cooperative businesses are also collected. Since then, researchers of cooperation in the country have had a center to develop theories and implement them, and the fact that the domestic cooperative movement has made overall progress has also been developed as a result.

Recently, the society has also communicated with cooperative organizations in various countries in order to seek assistance. At the same time, Chen is in charge of the investigation department, and conducts on-site investigations of rural economies and existing cooperative organizations in various provinces, in order to implement them step by step. At that time, the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Zhili, and Hebei received economic assistance from the provincial governments and Sino-foreign charity organizations. Farmers also tried cooperative organizations. The society first started the investigation from the four provinces. After two years, it was able to achieve the expected goals. During that time, Chen's trip to Hebei Province was with Hou Zhezang. The society, with the powerful evidence of theory and practice, has been more determined to carry out its business. In October 1930, it convened a general meeting of members in Hangzhou to announce the implementation plan of the Chinese cooperative movement. The plan was appropriate, but most of it relied on government facilities. In recent years, there have been domestic and foreign troubles, and the country has been troubled, which has been delayed. However, the society has not slackened in the part that it can do. In March 1931, it re-established the training class for cooperative staff in Nanjing, strictly defined the admission qualifications, and provided practical guidance. It took six months to graduate, and the employers were satisfied with the hired graduates in various places.

The society has also entrusted Jiang Ji as a resident officer in the United Kingdom, so as to closely connect with the International Cooperative Alliance and the British Cooperative Federation. Then, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture sent a letter to the society to preside over the cooperative affairs in Wu County, an experimental area. The society first recommended Wang Shiying and Chen Zhongming to negotiate the regulations of the experimental area with the Department of Agriculture, and then recommended Chen Zhongming, Li An, and Hou Houpei to be responsible for the cooperative organization and business technology guidance in the area. At that time, the director of the area, Hu Changling, worked hard, so the results were very satisfactory. In the autumn of 1931, the society re-established the Cooperative Issues Discussion Group to specifically study the problems that arise at any time in the implementation of domestic cooperation. Although it is not easy to gather the members who are scattered, but because of the vast area of China and the great differences in the situation, there are many things that need to be studied. This kind of specialized gathering is indeed a necessary facility.

In view of the increasing development of the cooperative business in our country, it is necessary to organize a joint association to engage in cooperative trade. Therefore, a Chinese Cooperative Wholesale Department was established this autumn to purchase quality goods on behalf of cooperative societies, or to sell products on behalf of cooperative societies, so as to form a formal cooperative federation step by step. It has not been long since its establishment, but the business is quite impressive.

In September of this year, the society felt that there were many cooperative businesses in various countries that could be used as a reference, so it raised funds to send member Peng Buzhu to Europe to conduct a thorough investigation of the countries that Chen Zhongming had not visited before, such as Germany, Belgium, Switzerland, and Italy, for reference.

In addition to cooperative business, the activity of its members is also remarkable. Now the members are all over the north and south, and the administrative organs and public organizations of cooperative businesses in various provinces are mostly presided over by members. There are also 273 members, 10 kinds of publications in large series, 19 kinds in small series, 4 kinds of popular ones, and the monthly magazine has been published to the tenth issue of the fourth volume. The special issues on specialized issues, such as the Cooperative Implementation Issue and the Cooperative Legislation Issue, are of great value. The most recent Rural Economy Issue is dedicated to discussing the current problems of the difficulties, which can be used for the reference of the people of the country.

In terms of its organization, under the Executive Committee, there are four departments for publicity, research, investigation, and guidance (and now a General Affairs Department). There are currently seven executive members and three alternate members. The standing committee members are Chen Guofu, Hou Houpei for general affairs, Wang Shiying for publicity, Shou Miancheng for research, Chen Zhongming for investigation, and Zhang Yan for guidance. The society is now located in the Lishui Villa on Shangji Yexi Road, and its wholesale department is attached to the Xinhua Trust and Savings Bank for convenience. Moreover, the society has purchased land in Nanjing, and if the society's affairs develop, it will build its own clubhouse, which can be expected soon.

The past four years of the society are briefly described above. In short, there are not many members and the funding is not sufficient, but it has been working on the cooperative business from ideal to implementation, from abroad to home. Meng Jin is commendable. Social people's livelihood and economy are the basis of the country. At this time when agricultural production is declining and people's livelihood is exhausted, the people of the country expect even more from the society to actively carry out the work and not disappoint the people of the country.

Local News Two

Chief Wang Investigates a Recorder for Interfering in Lawsuits 195

Recorder colludes with lawyers

Disputes arise over public fees

First Special Court concludes investigation

Commendable efforts by the court to rectify discipline

Huang Chengxie, a recorder at the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, is from Huzhou, Zhejiang, and resides at No. 345 Dong Tangjia Lane. He practices medicine. After becoming a recorder, he was assigned to the Criminal Simple Court, where he transcribed judgments every day when the court was in session. On the morning of May 27th of this year, before the court was about to hear the case of electricity theft by the China Hotel, lawyer Jiang Chiping received a phone call at his residence from Liang Bingchao, a translator at the Special Court (Liang and Jiang are good friends), saying that someone had entrusted him to appear in court for defense. Lawyer Jiang then drove to the court to meet Liang. It was a little after 8 a.m., and the judge had not yet taken the bench, but Zhang Deqing, the manager of the China Hotel, and Zhao, the hotel's inspector, were already waiting in the Simple Court. At this time, Huang Chengxie asked Zhang Deqing if the lawyer he had requested had arrived in court. Therefore, he pointed to lawyer Jiang and said to Zhang, "The lawyer you requested has arrived." The original lawyer Zhang requested was Jiang Yiping, and Jiang and Zhang knew each other. Logically, Zhang should have realized the mistake after seeing Jiang and not interact with each other. However, Zhang did not do so. He quickly approached Jiang, exchanged names, and learned that he was the client introduced by Liang. He immediately handed over a letter of appointment and had Zhang sign it. As soon as he finished signing, the judge opened the court. Therefore, Jiang and Zhang had no time to talk about anything else besides exchanging names. After the electricity theft case was concluded, lawyer Jiang requested 100 taels of silver from Liang for public fees that had been orally agreed upon when Liang introduced him. Liang said that Huang Chengxie had entrusted the matter to him, so he ordered Huang to ask Zhang for it. However, Zhang said that he had not entrusted lawyer Jiang. The person he asked that day was actually lawyer Jiang, who had already been hired. When he signed the letter of appointment, he was suspicious that lawyer Jiang might be representing Jiang because he did not have time to attend. He insisted that he did not want to pay. Later, after someone mediated, Zhang gave 50 yuan to Huang for transfer, and Liang transferred it to lawyer Jiang. However, Huang still thought it was not enough and often argued with Zhang Deqing, saying that no matter what, others had helped. Why should you cross the bridge and pull it down? If the public fees are not supplemented, gifts should be given as gifts. However, Zhang absolutely did not want to sacrifice a bit. The dispute has been going on until now, and it has not been resolved for four months. Recently, the matter was heard by Wang Zhennan, the chief prosecutor of the Second Branch of the High Court. He believed that Huang, as a court employee, interfered in external affairs, which was illegal. He secretly sent a prosecutor to the China Hotel twice, on September 28th and the 3rd of this month, to inquire about the situation and examine the important account books in the court. He then ordered the First Special District Local Court Prosecutor's Office to investigate strictly. The Local Prosecutor's Office took Huang Chengxie into custody on the 4th. At the same time, Prosecutor Zhang Guang led the clerk and bailiff to Huang's house in Dong Tangjia Lane at 5:30 p.m. on the same day to search. A full set of opium smoking tools was seized, and a trial was held once. Yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock, Prosecutor Zhang summoned Zhang Deqing, Jiang Chiping, and Xu Tongxiang, the current manager of the China Hotel, to continue the trial of Huang Chengxie. First, lawyer Jiang stated that he had received a phone call from translator Liang at home on the morning of May 27th and went to the Simple Court to meet Liang. He learned that the China Hotel had asked me to defend the electricity theft case and agreed on a public fee of 100 taels. Then Zhang Deqing signed the letter of appointment. Because the court was in session, there was no other talk except for exchanging names. I did not know Huang Zhang, but Huang was really present at the time. Then Zhang Deqing stated that he had gone to court that day and Huang had pointed him to meet lawyer Jiang. Lawyer Jiang ordered me to sign, and then I realized the misunderstanding. I paid Jiang a public fee of 50 yuan. Later, Huang came to order me to send gifts. Huang Chengxie confessed that he had told Zhang that lawyer Jiang had arrived because Zhang had asked about the lawyer that day. Later, Zhang sent insufficient legal fees, so he asked Zhang to send gifts. As for the confiscated smoking tools, he claimed that they belonged to his uncle. After the trial, it was announced that the investigation was over, and the defendant was returned to custody. Then the court adjourned.

Verdict in the Lizhong Lane Case 196

Indian murderer sentenced to ten years of hard labor

British Assessor General severely rebukes the murderer

A case in which Indian watchman You Sha of Lizhong Lane stopped three tenants, Hong Kaifa, from moving and stabbed Zhou A Yu to death was re-tried by British Assessor General Grahame after separately hiring jurors. The trial was completed yesterday afternoon, and You Sha was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment and hard labor. According to this case, after questioning the testimonies of both parties in the past two days, the court opened yesterday morning, and the prosecuting inspector and the defendant's lawyer debated the case. The Royal Inspector Mo Su summarized the testimonies and said that although the defendant claimed self-defense, he stabbed a person who had no weapons in his hand. If he claimed self-defense, he must prove that he had tried his best to avoid giving a fatal injury. Then the defendant's lawyer, Livingston, defended, still claiming self-defense, saying that the defendant's cane was held by the deceased, and he was afraid that his physical safety was in danger. After the debate was over, the jury retired to discuss, and immediately declared that the defendant was guilty. Then Assessor General Grahame sentenced him to ten years of imprisonment.

When Assessor General Grahame announced the verdict, he also said that the criminal had injured a young man who was only 21 years old. The jury's verdict was very lenient. The Assessor General severely rebuked the Indians for abusing sharp weapons and strictly ordered that this should not happen again in the future. After this punishment, he hoped that the same crime would not happen again.

An old woman was burned to death in a fire on Gordon Road 197

Catching bed bugs caused a fire

The old woman insisted on not escaping and lost her life

At about 4 a.m. yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out at No. 923 and a half Taile Lane, Gordon Road. The fire was very fierce at the time, spreading to the floors of the two neighbors on the left and right, and burning to death an old woman, Zhang Kong, 58 years old, who lived in the front building of the house with her daughter-in-law, Zhang. Her son was working outside, so he did not stay at home. Recently, the old woman was sick and lying in bed. Yesterday morning, the old woman felt strangely uncomfortable and suspected that there were bed bugs. She took a foreign candle and caught bed bugs around the bed before dawn. However, a sick person was weak, so she fell and the candle burned on the tent. When her daughter-in-law woke up from her dream, she quickly got out of bed and saw black smoke filling the room. She planned to escape with her mother-in-law, but the old woman insisted on not agreeing. Her daughter-in-law escaped alone and woke up the four neighbors. Later, someone reported that the fire brigade immediately drove the leather belt car to the scene and put out the fire. However, three houses had been burned down. The body of the old woman was dug out by the earthwork. Her head and face were burnt and her intestines flowed out. The situation was very miserable and unbearable to see. The Putuo Road Patrol House ordered the detectives to investigate. The body was carried to the Shuanglun Road inspection office. Yesterday morning, Zhang Lin Guang, a prosecutor from the First Special District Local Court, came to the office to verify the body. According to the testimony of the corpse's daughter-in-law, Zhang, when she saw the fire and the black smoke was very thick, she planned to drag her to escape together, but she resolutely refused and could not be rescued. Zhang got the testimony, and then announced that Zhang Kong, a dead woman, was verified to have been burned to death by fire during her lifetime. The body was handed over to her daughter-in-law to make a settlement for the coffin.

Minhang Ferry on Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway Completed 198

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway will be officially opened after the Double Tenth Festival. However, due to the large-scale bridge construction project in Minhang Huangpu, it has been decided to use ferries temporarily. The ferry was designed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities on behalf of the National Economic Commission. The first design by the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities cost about 50,000 yuan and took about half a year. However, due to the funds and time not being allowed, it was redesigned. It is said that the first designed ferry was a two-way type. Cars can drive into the ferry from both ends. From the bow to the stern, it can hold five or six cars. The second designed ferry is smaller, 15 meters long, 5.5 meters wide, and 2 meters high, with a draft of 1 meter. It is equipped with a diesel engine with an actual horsepower of 50 horsepower. It can travel 5.5 nautical miles per hour. The machine costs 11,636 yuan and was purchased from Qianxin Foreign Firm. The hull costs 13,700 yuan and was built by the Hexing Machine Manufacturing Factory. It was completed and delivered on the 1st of this month and has been tested in Minhang.

Hangzhou Municipal Government Favors Shanghai Automobiles 199

No need to install direction indicators

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities believes that the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Highway will be opened to traffic on the Double Tenth Festival. It is said that the Hangzhou Municipal Government requires all cars traveling in the city to be equipped with direction indicators (that is, to indicate the direction when the car turns). However, Shanghai cars do not have this kind of signal device. It is deeply feared that it will hinder communication after arriving in Hangzhou. Therefore, the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration was entrusted to negotiate with the Hangzhou Municipal Government. It is learned that the Hangzhou Municipal Government has agreed not to crack down on cars coming from Shanghai that are not equipped with various Hangzhou city signals.

Before the war, heavy troops were stationed in Paotai Bay, Wusong, because the place was an important pass and had to be strictly guarded. Since the agreement was signed to destroy the fortress without leaving any trace, there are now only thirty or forty soldiers in police uniforms stationed there. The Arrest of the Bandit Who Shot Police Officer Sun Jiming, Handed Over to the Public Security Bureau Yesterday 207

The First Special Court Sentenced Him to Five Years in Another Case

Liu Junqing, a Chinese detective from the Old Zhabei Police Station, had previously learned that a gang of bandits was hiding at No. 504 Chongqing Road. They arrested Wang Zhaosheng from Hebei and Li Decuan from Shandong, and confiscated a pistol, seven bullets, and a bayonet. They were handed over to the First Special Court for interrogation. Yesterday morning, Judge Qian Hongye of the Criminal Court continued the interrogation. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, stated that the police station is now prosecuting according to the regulations on prohibiting military firearms. However, they were caught before they could act. The police station found that on July 28th of this year, the defendant Wang Zhaosheng colluded with several other bandits to rob a cigarette paper store on Liyuan Road, near Xinqiao Road, in the city. Unexpectedly, as they approached the location, a police officer, Sun Jiming, attempted to search them. Wang and the others, seeing the situation was not good, immediately fired a shot, wounding Sun's left leg. A police officer named Zhang Hanchen happened to pass by and blew his whistle upon seeing the situation. Wang fired two more shots, hitting Zhang in the chest, killing him instantly. Sun's Mauser pistol was also taken by Wang and the others. Therefore, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau has sent personnel to the case, requesting transfer. It is requested to rule accordingly. Subsequently, Shen, an inspector from the Public Security Bureau, submitted an official document requesting transfer. When questioned, Li Decuan confessed to planning to rob his father-in-law's silver dollars. Wang Zhaosheng did not deny shooting the police officer from the Public Security Bureau, admitting that he fired the shots. Li Decuan hired lawyer Fan Gang for defense. Judge Qian reviewed the confessions and sentenced Wang Zhaosheng to five years in prison and Li Decuan to four years in prison. The pistol, bullets, and bayonet were all confiscated. Wang Zhaosheng was allowed to be taken away by personnel from the Public Security Bureau to be tried. After the verdict, they were sent back to this court for execution.

A Case of Fratricide Suddenly Unfolds 210

Ma Yuangui's Body Examined

Ding Mingcai Sent to Court for Legal Proceedings

Ma Yuangui, a barber from Zhenjiang, 32 years old, and Ding Mingcai, also from Zhenjiang and in the same trade, 52 years old, were close friends. They had previously opened a barbershop in Vladivostok as partners. Later, Ma transferred his shares to Ding and came to Shanghai alone. He is currently working as an employee at the Yingji barbershop at No. 12 Yuxing Street, French Concession. Ding came to Shanghai from Vladivostok and arrived on the 30th of last month. He stayed at the Yixinli Tongyizan on Lao Yong’an Street in the French Concession, inviting Ma to play and stay overnight with him every day. Ding planned to return to his native Zhenjiang on the 5th of this month and asked Ma to accompany him to the train station. The two were very affectionate. For some unknown reason, Ding suddenly lured Ma to the alley of Yixinli on Lao Yong’an Street at 11:00 PM on the 4th, took out a sharp blade, and stabbed Ma nine times in the arms and abdomen, causing his intestines to spill out and blood to flow profusely. Ding immediately fled. Ma, wounded, fled to the Huangpu Beach of Xinkaihe. The police found him, took him to the police station, and learned the details. The police chief ordered him to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. These details have already been briefly reported. It is now known that detectives discovered Ding hiding in Room 37 of the Chunjiang Inn at No. 318 Shangrenli, Guangdong Road, Public Concession. They immediately went with Chinese and Western detectives from the Public Concession Police Station, arrested Ding, and brought him back to the police station. The next day, he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. After questioning, Ding admitted to committing the assault and stabbing Ma. The court ordered him to be detained pending further questioning after the victim recovered from his injuries. Ma died of his serious injuries at 6:00 AM on the 6th. The court notified the police station and sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall autopsy room. At the same time, Li Weilong, the owner of the Yingji barbershop, telegraphed Ma Yuanqing, the deceased's brother, to come to Shanghai. Yesterday, Deng Baosun, the prosecutor of the Second Special Court, and the coroner arrived at the location, confirmed the body, took their seats at the court table, and according to the report from the patrol officer, the official briefly questioned the deceased's brother, and then ruled that Ma Yuangui had died from stab wounds. In addition to the Police Department sending the defendant to court for legal proceedings, the body was handed over to the deceased's brother, Ma Yuanqing, to collect and bury.

Buyer of the Auctioned British Ship "Bolchite" 227

Mr. Martin Purchased It for 50,000 Taels

The Shanghai Times reported that the British ship "Bolchite" (1658 tons) was confiscated by the Customs because it transported greyhound runners to Shanghai from Australia. Yesterday (the 6th), it was auctioned by Mr. Green of the River Conservancy. The initial bid was 30,000 taels. Then, Mr. Martin of the Ruihe Auction House increased it to 33,000 taels. Green saw that no one was bidding, so he announced that Customs had set the price at 50,000 taels. Then, Mr. Martin offered 50,000 taels, and no one continued to increase the price. Therefore, it was decided that Mr. Martin purchased it.

Siberia Transit 231

The Last Batch of Overdue Mail Arrives in Shanghai

According to postal sources, the last batch of overdue mail transited through Siberia arrived by train from Beijing and Shanghai on Thursday (October 7th). The dates of dispatch from London were August 2nd to 4th and 6th (the 7th was Sunday). The dates of dispatch from Paris were August 2nd to 4th, and the dates of dispatch from Berlin were August 3rd to 7th. All previously reported missing mail transited through Siberia has now been completely received. Also, on that day, 33 bags of European mail were received from Bangalore via the Suez Canal, including mail dispatched from London on September 1st and from Paris on September 2nd.

On the same day last year, the highest was 86.0 degrees, and the lowest was 68.0 degrees.

Letter to the Editor 247

To the Editor:

Regarding the news item "Four Criminals Captured in Concession, Identified by Wu Guangzong's Family" on page 15 of your newspaper on the 4th of this month, there are some discrepancies with the facts. The criminal Yao Jiechen, who was captured this time, has long lived in Hongxingqiao, Changxing, and has committed numerous crimes, which are widely known. He is indeed significantly involved in the Changxing coal mine robbery. The other three criminals, Song Jiande, Wu Jigui, and Zhang Shaoliang, are also major suspects in this case. Our unit has been investigating and pursuing them for nearly a year, using all possible means. We finally learned that the criminals were hiding in Shanghai. On September 29th, we sent Detective Li Nianyun, along with informant Zhou Mingshan, carrying official documents to Shanghai. We first secretly monitored the criminals. At 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the 30th, we reported to the Laozha Police Station of the British Concession and, in cooperation with Chinese Detective Pang Yutang and Western Detective Los, captured Song Jiande and Wu Jigui, two Henan natives, at No. 89 Jue Lu Hotel on Xizang Road. They confessed on the spot to the whereabouts of the remaining accomplices, who were staying at Room 28 of the Xindahua Hotel on Fuzhou Road. We went to that location and captured Yao Jiechen and Zhang Shaoliang. Western Detective Los then found two Mauser pistols, two handguns, and thirty-nine bullets. The suspects and the loot were taken to the Laozha Police Station for temporary detention. On the morning of October 1st, at 9:00 AM, the suspects were transferred to the Special District Court, where they were interrogated by Judge Ma Shide of the Criminal Division, who ordered a week-long review. This is the actual situation at the time. We fear that rumors and misinformation will confuse the public, so we are sending this letter to clarify the truth and request that you make a correction promptly. We appreciate your cooperation.

Sincerely,

Headquarters of the 2nd Regiment of the Zhejiang Provincial Security Force

October 6th

To the Editor:

On the evening of October 1st, the Qing Tian surveying ship, under our bureau's command, was anchored at the Bajiang Port on the Yangtze River, at 31 degrees 56 minutes 30 seconds north latitude and 120 degrees 14 minutes 10 seconds east longitude. At 10:30 PM, the Jiangyu merchant ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was sailing downstream. After stopping there to unload passengers, it switched to turning the wheel. It did not prevent the speed of the rapids flowing down, causing the ship's left side of the bow to collide with the Qing Tian ship's bow. Although the Qing Tian ship first unloaded the chain, it was too late. At the time, the ship's bow and stern lights were bright. Therefore, after the collision, the Jiangyu captain immediately admitted his negligence, filled out a certificate, and sent it to the Qing Tian ship as a basis for compensation. However, the Shanghai newspapers stated that the Qing Tian ship did not have its lights on, which is completely inconsistent with the facts. We are sending this letter in the hopes that you will publish it to clarify the facts. Your assistance is greatly appreciated.

Sincerely,

Hydrographic Office of the Naval Department

October 6th

Regarding yesterday's newspaper report that Communist leaders Hu Gongyuan and others were hiding upstairs in the Minmin Primary School at No. 469 Minhou North Lane, Hardoon Road, and were arrested by the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station, it is truly unfortunate. Tracing back to the afternoon of August 10th of this year, a Miss Chen, about twenty years old, and her friend came to rent a room, claiming that "her father works in the Nanjing Municipal Government and that there are three in the family, a mother and two daughters." They rented a vacant room and lived there for more than two weeks. A man, about forty years old, came to live with them. Upon detailed inquiry, the daughter replied "Father," with the name "Anshi," who was "working in Nanjing and has now returned to Shanghai for business." Unexpectedly, this incident occurred two weeks later. Fearing that the outside world does not understand the truth, we are stating the whole story and sending this letter to your newspaper, requesting a correction. Your assistance will be greatly appreciated.

Sincerely,

Jin Chengde, Principal of Minmin Primary School

Free Talk

Aphorisms of Ma Xiangbo, a Nonagenarian

Hope of the Nation! 248

— Jing Ji

Around the Double Tenth National Day, a special speech on the so-called "Hope of the Nation" was delivered.

China's only hope at present is truly patriotic youth! I remember Old Man Xiang met with the leaders of the Chinese Youth Party at the Leshan Hall and sincerely said:

"The current political stage in China lacks truly capable people. You are all young and strong, have studied abroad for many years, and naturally have a sense of the importance of patriotism! Moreover, you are willing to humbly learn and work practically! What can I say? Patriotism is based on love for others! Let me explain briefly, and I think you will understand. Because 'nation' is an abstract term, formed by the collective of 'people and people'; therefore, the people are the basic atoms or constituent elements of the nation.

You see the degradation of your compatriots and cannot bear to see them continue to be slaughtered. You call on young comrades to unite and save the country: this is the spirit of universal love and saving people! This is truly the so-called 'Hope of the Nation!'

In the past, autocratic emperors and militarists of large empires not only ate the people's offerings but also consumed the people themselves! They squeezed and sucked every drop of the people's blood. Their families, children, and wealth did whatever they pleased, harming both themselves and the nation! I ask: after you come to power, will you continue to act in the same way? If you do not love the people and the nation at that time, then it is better not to engage in this political business from the beginning!

You are humble and ask for my guidance, saying that you will still treat me with the respect of a disciple as you did a dozen years ago. Your virtue is admirable! I am old, and I hope that you will use your sincere love for others to strive to save the country. Like 'leaven,' you will succeed! I don't say much, but a little leaven, when added to three dou of flour, will quickly rise and expand! Hundreds of thousands of comrades can be spread across the country! The gospel of love for others is consistent, and the spirit of patriotism is the same: may you, lovely young people, remember this!"

Timely Words for the Double Ninth Festival 249

— Zhu Gai

Ascending Heights and Sending Wine

Ascending Heights: In the past, Huan Jing followed the instructions of an immortal. On the Double Ninth Festival, he led his wife and children to ascend to a high place to avoid disaster. When they returned, their house was indeed empty, and all their chickens and dogs were dead. Now, our compatriots in the Northeast are struggling and groaning in their devastated homeland, trampled by the iron hooves of the enemy. The people within the country are suffering from the slaughter of bandits in the interior and the infighting of warlords in the border regions. Calamities are everywhere, and there are refugees everywhere. How dangerous! If we don't ascend to a high place soon, we will truly be in danger of disaster. No wonder the crowns of important people can be found everywhere on the mountain tops even before the Double Ninth Festival.

Sending Wine: During the Double Ninth Festival, Mr. Jingjie sat facing chrysanthemums, with not a drop of wine in his pot. In this impoverished environment, a white-clad man carrying a jar full of wine came to deliver it. This is an act of giving charcoal in the snow, so it is no wonder that Mr. Jingjie got drunk. Our volunteer army in the Northeast is fighting for the glory of the nation and the victory of the country. Under the iron hooves, they are desperately fighting. How admirable and moving! But those who die in battle are indeed lying dead on the battlefield, and those who are captured will suffer the inhumanity of being beheaded by the puppet regime. I think that any Chinese with a little conscience will hardly watch them and the Northeast rivers and mountains perish together. Then the volunteer army lacks both bullets and food, and is in such a difficult environment. People of the country, be generous! If you have not forgotten the scars of January 28th, quickly learn from the white-clad man sending wine and donate some money to the volunteer army. Don't wait until after the country is lost, when there will be no money to donate!

Buddhist Shop 250

— Chi Fo

Business with No Capital

Indeed, Shanghai is a world where gold is everywhere. Silver dollars are rolling around on the streets. Those who are fortunate have the possibility of enjoying them; those who are not fortunate will instead have their shoes pierced! Therefore, the past histories of many celebrities are often not very pleasant to talk about because they have sharp minds and a spirit of struggle, and have become lucky people.

But as of now, there are not many silver dollars rolling around on the streets, and it is very difficult to find them, so everyone is bound to panic. A friend said to me: "Now there is a business that will guarantee you make a fortune, as long as you hire a

Impression of Mr. Liu Haisu by Liu Yazi 251

I have known Haisu for six years, but I heard his name probably ten years before that. The model case of 1914 left me with the deepest impression. This was a conflict between art and etiquette, that is, a struggle between the emerging bourgeois consciousness in backward countries in the East and the feudal system that had already declined but had not yet been completely eradicated.

In 1927, I met him for the first time in Inokashira Park outside Tokyo, Japan, but we were both living a life of exile. At this time, the authorities probably thought that my thinking was too left-leaning, and that I was some kind of suspect; and for Haisu, they thought he was too right-wing, and added the title of academic warlord. It's so difficult to be a person, isn't it? We laughed as soon as we met. So we talked about politics, literature, Fielun, and Manshu, with great interest. After drinking, I wrote two poems and sent them to him:

(1) Meeting overseas is extraordinary, after ten years of fame, we are both old and weary. A volume of Fielun's collected works is there, and we talked about Su Lang, the wild goose and the departing geese. (2) The white-clothed man sent wine to Tao Yuanliang, and Zao Mao lived in the Yi Guan Youan. A smile advises you to shut up, the chickens and dogs in the world are all south of the Huai River. A few days later, I went to the Asahi Shimbun to visit his solo exhibition. Haisu's works are great, and I don't need to introduce them. What I paid special attention to that day was the inscription on his works, from Kang Changsu, Le Ren'gong to Hu Shih, Guo Moruo, almost like a list of modern Chinese celebrities. My favorite one had a sentence by Moruo, and the content was truly magnificent. You want to match Moruo's bold and strong poetic writing with Haisu's majestic and broad sketches. Isn't it the best in the world? The impression of this day was simply overwhelming.

After I returned to China in 1928, my contact with Haisu became sparse. Haisu went to Europe in 1929 and traveled to France, Italy, Germany, Belgium, Switzerland and other countries. It was not until 1931 that he returned to Shanghai. His progress in the past three years is of course limitless, but his attitude towards people has not been arrogant. On September 4, 1932, his nephew, Liu Shi, held a solo exhibition at the China Art Society. I went to visit, and he and his wife, Ms. Zhang Yunshi, both came out to greet me warmly. This kind of artistic family harmony is very likely to win the warm sympathy of the general public.

Now, the municipal government wants to host an exhibition of his European works. In order to print the garden from memory as a memorial, I wrote a preface on it for Suwo. Writing a preface is not an easy thing, especially since I am a complete layman when it comes to art. However, my history of meeting Haisu overseas is an unforgettable one. I will write this impression as a preface. The talks about the Buddha's head being dung are of course inevitable. Haisu will consider whether to use it or not.

Shanghai, September 27, 1932

partner, and you don't need much start-up capital or decoration. The best thing is that the hired partner doesn't need a salary, doesn't need to eat, and there is no risk of a strike. Where in the world is there such a good business!" I was very surprised when I heard this. That friend said: "Don't be surprised, isn't opening a Buddhist shop the best business in Shanghai?"

Later, I thought about it carefully, and this sentence is not wrong at all. In addition to the so-called "Lower Court" and "Branch Court" in Shanghai, there are also many "Buddhist Shops," inside which there are no monks, nuns, or Taoists, but only a statue of a Buddha! This is the partner acting as a facade. The owner of the Buddhist shop must have a master, such as Huatuo, Huang Shigong, Han Xiangzi, Zhang Guniang, Lord Cao, etc. The master often drills into the owner's belly. Treating diseases, practicing spiritism, fortune-telling, communicating with the dead, asking about good and bad luck, and even national events and Sino-Japanese negotiations can be predicted. When the master comes, the owner yawns greatly, cries and drools, and behaves ugly, which is both annoying and funny.

The sister-in-law in the attic lost the flower meeting, and unintentionally heard someone mumbling and saying in the vegetable market while buying vegetables: "Lord Cao is really effective! Yesterday he said to open 'Zheng Bide,' and it was indeed correct. I won thirty yuan." Two people on a certain bus were talking loudly, gesticulating and saying: "The Huatuo Altar in XX Li X is really effective in treating diseases! My brother has been blind for five years, and both Chinese and Western medicine can't cure it. Eight Friends from the Post Office (8) 252

— Qiu Xingfu Zhai Zhu

Then the two entered the English Clothing School. Tong Yizhen still attended the clothing class from 8:00 to 10:00 as usual, and Lu Boqin also took care of everything from the side. "Are you sure you're going to Wan Quan tomorrow?" She asked firmly.

"I'm definitely going," he replied.

"Then, you don't have to send me. Go back to sleep quickly, don't overthink things, and especially don't be too concerned about the pros and cons. It's difficult for things in the world to have all the advantages and no disadvantages. If you think this matter is worth doing on the premise, then just boldly move forward and do it as far as you can. If you believe what I say, you will have a satisfactory answer to me tomorrow. I am eagerly looking forward to it." After she spat out these firm, steel-like words word by word, she strode away. But Lu Boqin was still hesitant and pondering as he went home, with no excitement or excitement like a warrior.

(2)

The next day, the two young men and women were indeed found in Wan Quan Park. This Wan Quan Park is located in the southeast corner outside of Fanyang City. Tourists can reach it by exiting the city from the Dananmen or Dadongmen. It was originally called Wan Quan River, with several weeping willows and a stream of water, with a bit of Jiangnan scenery. Later, it was developed into a park, with small bridges, winding paths, flower beds, and thatched pavilions added to embellish it, making it the only scenic spot in Shenyang. That year, the authorities in charge of municipal administration intended to make Wan Quan more clean and refined. They drove away all the motley, multi-faceted tents in the style of Shichahai in Beiping, and only allowed clean tea seats to be set up. Wan Quan had a different kind of seclusion and fame, and became a place for civilized ladies to stroll and have fun.

The market price is estimated at 28 taels per box. It is heard that the spot goods of foreign firms have been sold one after another in recent days, and there are not many in the market. Therefore, the market situation is very weak, and the market price is expected to continue to rise.

35-Pound Thin Tinplate Is Scarce 285

Recently, the spot goods of 35-pound thin factory tinplate have been very scarce, and the number of buyers from various gangs is relatively high. The market situation is generally getting more and more expensive, and it is estimated that each box can be estimated at 40 taels, which is an advance of two from the previous telegram.

Obey the Central Government 286

— Fo

Who! Dares to say that not obeying the central government's orders is a crime, is treasonous, and should be subject to appropriate punishment, so no one dares not to obey the central government's orders.

In the Shandong Han-Liu dispute, Han Fuju said, I obey the central government's orders. Liu Zhennian also said, I obey the central government's orders. However, up to now, Yexian, Laiyang and other places are still fighting fiercely. Does the central government order the two to kill each other? But they all said that they obeyed the central government's orders.

The Sichuan Second Liu dispute, although not yet opened, but the mediation is feared to be hopeless. According to Liu Wenhui, I obey the central government's orders, and Liu Xiang also said, I obey the central government's orders. However, according to Liu Xiang's representative Fan Chongshi, the Sichuan incident has the possibility of war, and according to Liu Cunhou's representative Yu Yun, the Sichuan war is unavoidable. In the end, are the two obeying the central government, or are they not obeying the central government? Since they have obeyed the central government, why do they still want to start a war? Since they have not obeyed the central government, why do they always say that they obey the central government?

The four words "obey the central government" are indeed a golden signboard of "uniformity and non-discrimination" and "honesty to the old and young." The quality of the goods in the store can be ignored. The weaker party relies on the signboard of obeying the central government in order to obtain the assistance of the central government. The stronger party relies on the signboard of obeying the central government. On the one hand, it can prevent the central government from assisting the weaker, and on the other hand, it can get rid of the crime of disobeying the central government's orders. In the same obedience to the central government's orders, each has its own psychology, and each has its own effect. This is a wonderful method of "disobeying the truth and escaping the blame" in recent days.

This method, if used properly, can be handled in this way regardless of the matter. Although saying "so and so," in fact, it can be "not so not so." It is really a so-called "hanging a sheep's head and selling dog meat." Selling it to six villages is six villages, and what reason can be asked? Therefore, most of the recent store sales are like this. The Japanese organization of the puppet Manchuria is nothing more than using this method. That is, all the methods of being a human being and being an official are nothing more than this. The two Lus are wonderfully different. Spring sells it. Everywhere this can be found. Alas! Obey the central government's orders! Obey the central government's orders! So many sins in the sky are committed in your name! Literature and Art
