Science

Glaze 288

— Ling Zhou

Ruan is a translucent thing. It is applied to increase beauty and make it waterproof. The method of manufacturing it is very complicated. Due to the limited space here, only the essentials are extracted and the operating procedures are described in order.

1. Pulverization of hard raw materials. The hard raw materials used in the glaze, such as quartz and feldspar, should first be made into extremely fine powder for application. There are two types of grinding methods: dry and wet. The dry type must pay attention to the dispersal of dust, which puts the operator in an unhealthy environment.

2. Mixing method. A. Fluxing agent. To make a glaze, first prepare a fluxing agent. Mix the ingredients according to their composition and mix them intimately. Then put it in a crucible, melt it into a liquid by baking at high temperature, and then take it out and quench it in water, or let it cool completely. It changes into irregular crystalline or solid shapes. B. Glaze grinding method. Add water and a suitable proportion of insoluble substances to the above-mentioned solvent that has been made, and put it in a stone ball crusher with a figure to grind it into an extremely fine slurry. The glaze is then formed. C. Composition. The following are the compositions of glaze for readers and those interested in ceramics to study. Fluxing agent Quartz 26 Boric acid 15 Lead oxide 1.9 16 Magnesite 11 Chalk 13 Glaze Fluxing agent 70 Feldspar 24

Page 21

White Lead 289

— Liu

The chemical formula of the above glaze composition is as follows. Three glaze application methods. The purpose of the already fired or unfired mud blank is completed by the following methods. A. Impregnation method. The object to be glazed is impregnated in a glaze of appropriate consistency to complete it. B. Pouring method. The glaze is poured onto the utensils to be glazed. C. Brushing method. Use objects such as brushes to brush the glaze on the utensils. D. Air pressure method. This method is the most popular method at present. Not only can the work be quick, but also the glaze can be made evenly thick. The method uses air pressure to push the glaze out from extremely fine holes. After exiting, it becomes a smoke and attaches to the utensils. E. Volatilization method. This method is made by the action of salt, metal and steam. That is, the action of salt and steam decomposes into soda and hydrochloric acid. The reaction is as follows:

2NaC1+H20=Na20+2HC1 In this way, steam and hydrochloric acid each escape, and the remaining soda then combines with the silicic acid in the mud blank, which is a bright salt glaze on the utensils.

Finally, we must pay attention to whether the expansion and contraction force of the mud blank and the glaze is consistent. If they are not consistent, the applied glaze will inevitably expand or contract and crack. If the expansion and contraction force of the glaze is greater than that of the mud blank, then the amount of aluminum oxide (AiK ll) must be reduced and boric acid must be increased, such as the basic silicic acid of the aluminum oxide class. The largest expansion and contraction force of each raw material is aluminum oxide (NA20=100, K20=8.5) (Note). The smallest one is silicic acid (S102=0.8) (Note).

(Note) See Winklenannandscbottsafactors Table

Social Improvement Discussion Meeting

Opinions on Improving "Sending Sentiments" 290

— Ci Min

The problem of sending sentiments has always troubled me. For the past few days, I have been thinking about proposing suggestions in this publication to discuss an improved approach with everyone. Unexpectedly, Mr. Zicai's great work was submitted and published in this publication before mine, which can truly be said to be "exactly what I had in mind." Humans are emotional creatures, so interpersonal interactions often revolve around "sentiment." When relatives and friends have joyous occasions or losses, it is necessary to express "sentiment" of congratulations or condolences to them. However, "sentiment" is inherently an internal spiritual function. How can I express this "sentiment"? How can I make relatives and friends sense or accept the "sentiment" I am expressing to them? Everyone feels that it is somewhat difficult to fulfill this task solely through "sentiment" itself. Thus, the practice of using tangible material gifts to express "sentiment" arose. Therefore, the problem of sending sentiments, as Mr. Zicai mentioned, has evidently transformed into a "problem of sending gifts" in the present day.

"A goose feather sent from a thousand miles away, the gift is light but the sentiment is heavy." It should be understood that the quantity of gifts is by no means a measure of the weight of sentiment. Mr. Zicai said, "However, to express sentiment, grandiosity is not necessary," which is indeed true. However, in this society where the spiritual and material are separated, in a capitalist society where most people adhere to extreme "fetishism," the chain relationship between "gift" and "sentiment" is often broken in many situations. The phenomenon of gift-giving need not originate from "sentiment," and "unprovoked gifts" can be given to achieve certain purposes. Conversely, between parties with "sentiment" relationships, the phenomenon of gift-giving may not necessarily accompany it due to the driving force of "the whip of snobbery." There are many such examples, so I won't go into detail. Now, let's set aside these abnormal facts and discuss my limited view on improving this problem. In addition to agreeing with Mr. Zicai's opinion, I feel that two points should be added: First, the closeness of sentiment should be the criterion for sending sentiments. For example, if my long-time teacher dies, even if his family does not send me a notice, I should send sentiments to express my deep sorrow. Also, for example, if my teacher's grandparents or parents die, even if they send me a notice, I may not need to send sentiments, because there is no "sentiment" to speak of between me and those people.

Second, reduce the number of occasions for sending sentiments. Weddings, betrothals, funerals, and burials are major events in life. Sending sentiments for celebration or condolences is appropriate. But looking at the current occasions for sending sentiments in society, they are truly diverse and complicated, such as the completion of a new house! Or a son's birthday! And what else...! Layer upon layer, more and more. If sentiments have to be sent for everything, wouldn't we poor scholars be driven to death! For the sake of the general public, reducing the occasions for sending sentiments is even more necessary.

What do you think, Mr. Zicai? What do you think, readers?

Casual Talk

Words on the Tip of the Tongue 291

— Zeng Yu

In the process of love between men and women, men often succumb to women. After marriage, women gradually succumb to men.

People who have received higher education are not necessarily all of noble character. People who have not received education are not necessarily all despicable.

If people can use the determination and courage of suicide to pursue any career, they are sure to succeed.

All evils in the world originate from a momentary mistake in people's consciences.

People who are good at scholarship and morality certainly obtain it from books, but some of the bad deeds done by villains also come from books.

When Chinese people have a skill, they want to show off their abilities everywhere. For example, those who understand law will use law to cite, argue, and explain when talking.

If young people can pursue learning with the perseverance and determination to seek love, their future achievements will be limitless.

When people yearn for something they have not obtained, their hope for it is very profound. But after they get it, they become indifferent and no longer cherish it.

When people are in extreme pain, they will not fantasize about everything in times of happiness. But when they are in extreme happiness, they should at least fear that sorrow is about to descend.

Those who test love are like the prospects of explorers, both are vague. At the same time, they are all praying for the development of new hope.

National crisis is like opium, it can only be tried once in a while, but the spirit is very exciting. Now the national crisis is so numerous that it cannot be counted, just like old addicts, even if they inhale a lot of opium, it is useless.

The fate of one's future is determined by oneself, and the same is true for a country.

Street Corners and Alleys

Random Records of a Stroll 292

— Wen Bing

—Listeners in the Auction—

Life is always so dry and dull, with no development to speak of, and my heart is already full of boredom. In order to breathe some new air, after lunch, I jumped out of my cage-like small room and slowly strolled to the northern part of North Sichuan Road, which is full of Cantonese flavor. This immediately reminded me of the Northeast under the iron hooves of Japanese imperialism, and the people of the North under the infighting between Han and Liu. It seemed that the prelude to "foreign invasion and internal strife" was unfolding before my eyes. My footsteps stopped, and I was by the book stall at the intersection of Haining Road. Looking around, I found a copy of the "May 30th Special Issue" of the Oriental Magazine. I casually asked the hawker,

"How much is this?"

"Four dimes!"

"Is two dimes okay?"

"No, it's exactly four small dimes!"

In fact, even two dimes, I couldn't take them out at the moment, so I just glanced at the content and left. A few steps forward was the Hongkou Grand Hotel, which had a reputation for its sturdy leather. It was now heavily locked with iron gates, and the broken bricks and tiles, broken glass, etc., were piled up here and there in a chaotic mess. I remembered visiting a friend there two years ago. Because my clothes were too shabby, the gatekeeper kept looking at me with suspicion, meaning: "You are either a beggar or a pickpocket!" It really made me feel resentful. Seeing its current destruction, I felt truly happy! But then I thought of the Japanese soldiers' tyranny, and finally my personal grudges were suppressed.

I strolled slowly again, and a series of drums and music of the usual price reduction and clearance sales came from the front. It turned out to be upstairs in a certain company at the corner. The entrance was crowded with people, packed like sardines. Driven by my desire to sightsee, I also pushed my way in. The first thing I noticed upon entering was the four big characters "Beware of Pickpockets" posted on a large piece of glass. I instinctively touched the pen in my pocket, and luckily it was still there. So I felt relieved and started to look around: It was indeed a big sale, hats, clothing materials, silk stockings, cosmetics, everything was very cheap. Unfortunately, my pockets were "empty as a suspended chime," so I could only look around and watch others picking and choosing, their hands full. A Cantonese woman with long braids bought a bottle of Shiseido's Thousand Mile Fragrance for two small dimes, a bottle of Samsung brand cologne for one dime, and two pairs of long silk stockings for four dimes each, and walked away with her eyes glazed over. There was also a heavily pregnant Bai Xiang friend with particularly long sleeves, who bought a hat that originally cost four dollars for one dollar and put it on his head. Also, many people always came empty-handed and left fully loaded. It was truly a rare opportunity for cheap goods. It's just that those goods were all stained with mud and ashes, and wrinkled. It turned out that they were moved out hastily during the "January 28th" incident, so they became like that! Dirty and wrinkled, so they were being auctioned off cheaply.

I think anyone with a little bit of conscience would be able to tell that those goods were not just mud and ashes, nor were they just wrinkles. They were all the tears of our compatriots, the blood of the soldiers of the 19th Route Army! Each customer who bought cheap goods should know that this was a gift from the Japanese soldiers during the "January 28th" incident! How should we thank them! Repay them!

A Corner of Society

War in the Mouth of a Pastor 293

— Ren

In this year of tragic and painful national crisis, whether young or old, everyone should be filled with enthusiasm and burning blood, holding guns and bayonets: charging and annihilating the enemy! Because, China, our motherland! Who would willingly watch their bright and lovely motherland sink and perish?

Is that so? Do the people of China all have such majestic aspirations and steadfast will? Friends! Hold on, let me tell you about a painful, sad, and infuriating thing I encountered during the national crisis!

Next to a wide road in western Shanghai, a solemn and magnificent X Church stood tall. On this day, it was the day when their believers were holding a gathering for worship and prayer. A returned from a memorial meeting at school and asked me to accompany him to visit the atmosphere of the church commemorating the national crisis.

Four legs stepped onto the steps, and a yellow-haired, blue-eyed foreigner flashed out of the house to welcome us, and cordially invited us. So we entered the last row of seats. The hall was divided into left and right sides, with four or five hundred men and women sitting, including fashionable young people and young ladies, as well as rural men and old women with local flavor. But the atmosphere inside was always very quiet and full of solemnity and dignity.

"When the national crisis is at hand, we need to fight!" A Western-dressed young pastor stood on the podium, gesticulating and talking about his (doctrine), "But, when you are preparing to fight, first, you often think that the Holy Spirit is with you; second, you must carry the cross of Jesus; third, you should hold the Lord's honey example. Then, you

Page 22

Victory is certain, and the enemy's artillery fire and flesh will be defeated at the sight because your war is our Lord fighting for you, and our Lord is so noble and great, with authority and love for us! We should thank our Lord and ask him to be with us forever, and our country will naturally become prosperous and strong..."

Holding our breath and sitting like pins and needles, we were almost suffocating to death, but still patiently endured and continued to listen to this so-called (doctrine) for two hours. Finally, amidst the smiling farewell of the foreigners, we slipped out onto the road, deeply inhaling a breath of fresh air, as if prisoners had been granted amnesty and were seeing the light of day again!

"Damn it, Jesus has his own reasons! A"

He said to himself with a bitter face. Then, he clenched his fists tightly and shouted in grief and indignation: "Foreign slaves, running dogs, damned things! Giant demons that anesthetize life, living corpses with frozen blood! It's rare that he still knows that "the country is in danger", and it's rare that he still knows that "we need to fight", but the Holy Spirit, the sword, the cross... A series of ghostly talks and nonsense, our country will naturally become prosperous and strong? Will the enemy's artillery fire and flesh really be defeated at the sight? What is the Lord? Can he fight for us? Friends, anesthetized friends! Wake up, stop being obsessed with the non-existent "authority of God", please abandon your narrow-minded individual heroism, let us unite our masses, concentrate the power of the masses, burn with enthusiasm, hold guns, and bayonets; charge, and annihilate the enemy! Kill, friends, kill! Kill! Fight! China, China is our motherland!"

Nonsense 294

Five Mr. "Dare Nots" Meng Jian Mr. is a common title, and anyone dares to accept it; but the following five Mr. are those that some people dare not accept. Because someone dares not be a Mr., I say they are five Mr. dare nots.

(1) Mr. Official The traditional ideology of a patriarchal society. Everyone is willing to be this Mr., but because Mr. Official often does bad things, some people dare not accept it. In fact, it is not that they dare not accept it, but that they cannot do it well or for long, and they express their unwillingness to accept it in their resignation letters.

(2) Mr. Nanguo The ones who fill the ranks. In practice, there are many who dare to accept it, but on the surface, no one dares to accept it. So now, those who are referred to as Mr. Nanguo dare not accept it, and those who can be Mr. Nanguo are lucky.

(3) Little Mr. Little Mr. is another name for a child prostitute. Becoming one is the first step into the fire pit, becoming a plaything for men, becoming the dregs of society, simply becoming a person without freedom. Those who are little Mr. have no concept of daring to accept, it is entirely due to being young and ignorant and being framed by others. If they have a little reason, a little life skills, and can escape the shackles of good people, I think they will definitely not dare to accept it.

(4) Mr. Guo This Mr. can be surnamed Guo, but people surnamed Guo will get angry when they hear it, thinking it is an insult, and they dare not accept it.

(5) Mr. Illiterate Everyone has been a Mr. Illiterate when they were young, but when they grow up, they dare not accept it, because they are afraid of being embarrassed if they do. There are many Mr. Illiterates now, but how exactly can they dare to accept it? I'll talk about it next time.

If the fine is not paid in full, it will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be offset by three yuan per day. Spring Palace books and samples are confiscated according to the list (Above October 7).

▲Civil Second Instance Judgment: Xi Changhao was sued by Jiudi Real Estate Company for refusing to accept the rent arrears case (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant. ▲ Su Mengtesheng was sued by Xu Yilin for refusing to accept the loan case (Main Text): The original judgment is changed. Xu Yilin should repay the appellant's loan of 200 yuan, deducting 20 yuan per month until it is repaid. If Xu Yilin is unable to repay, Xu Fulin will repay it on his behalf. The litigation costs of both instances are borne by Xu Yilin. ▲ Caimen sues Na Foxiao for refusing to accept the debt for goods (Main Text): The original judgment on the amount of repayment and litigation costs of the appellant is changed. The appellant should repay the appellee 350 yuan and 4 jiao. The appellant's appeal on the above parts and the appellee's remaining claims in the original trial are rejected. The first and second instance litigation costs, except for the parts withdrawn by the appellee, are borne by the appellant. ▲ Wang Jinzhuang refuses to accept the compensation case (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant. ▲ Yongli Company refuses to accept the rent arrears case (Main Text): All appeals are rejected. The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant in proportion. ▲ Zhang Hongfa refuses to accept the loan case (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant (Above October 7).

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 297

▲ Civil Judgment: Zou Renji vs. Gong Shengxuan et al. Guarantee Case (Main Text): The defendants shall, within seven days from the date of this judgment, hand over Wang Xia Shi, the person employed by the plaintiff. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants. ▲ Flaviir Keningko vs. Mattway Rakalov Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff a special remuneration fee of seventy-two yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from the date of the lawsuit until the end of enforcement. The remaining claims and the request for provisional execution by the plaintiff are dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear three-fifths of the litigation costs, and the defendant shall bear two-fifths. ▲ Wang Jinqing vs. Huang Lianfu Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 197.50 yuan. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Shanghai Silver Company vs. Ma Er: 318 yuan, litigation costs borne by the defendant. ▲ Tan Mao Yi Tang vs. Yuan Sheng Hao Rent Arrears and Eviction Case (Main Text): The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲ Prosecutor of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court vs. Mei Lai Nuowei Si Gai Check Debt (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff 100 yuan for the check, and shall pay 25 yuan for the check separately between the 1st and 10th of each month from October 1932 to July 1932. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Yuan Li vs. Zheng Xihou et al. Rent Case (Main Text): Defendant Zheng Xihou shall pay the plaintiff rent of 105 yuan. Defendant Lu Jinxiang shall pay the plaintiff rent of 63 yuan. Defendant Zhang Xuebing shall pay the plaintiff rent of 51 yuan. Litigation costs, excluding the settlement portion, shall be borne by the defendants proportionally. ▲ Qian Zhang Shi vs. Yu A Mao Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 500 yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of two percent from January 1, 1928, until the date of final execution. This amount is permitted to be paid in three installments, with one month as one period. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Bao Hua Company vs. Ling Heng Ji Firm Goods Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff a goods debt of 456.80 yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from the date of the lawsuit until the date of final execution, and permission is granted to pay this amount in two installments with one month as one period. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Zhang Wu Shi vs. Gen Tang Rent and Return of House Case (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 40 yuan and return House No. 8 inside No. 762 of Hongde Fang on Julai Road to the plaintiff. The remaining requests of the plaintiff are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. This judgment regarding the return of the leased house may be provisionally enforced. ▲ Zhou Ji Sheng Hao vs. Qing Feng Hao Zhang Qingyu Goods Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff a goods debt of silver 56 taels and 3 qian, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from January 6, 1931, until the date of final execution. The remaining requests of the plaintiff are dismissed. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Yihe Company vs. Chen Lianxi et al. Rent Case (Main Text): Defendants Chen Lianxi and Jin Tongfu shall each pay the plaintiff rent of 90 yuan and 15 jiao in small coins. Defendants Zhang Youliang and Wu A'wu shall each pay the plaintiff rent of 54 yuan and 9 jiao in small coins. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants proportionally. ▲ Yi Kang Feng Ji Zhuang, et al. vs. Heng Chang Ren Ji Tobacco Company, et al. Debt Case (Main Text): Heng Chang Sheng Ji Tobacco Company owes the plaintiffs a total of 50,963 taels, 5 qian, and 3 fen of iron, plus interest. Defendant Wang Leting shall be responsible for clearing and repaying the debt. The remaining requests of the plaintiffs are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiffs. ▲ Wu Zishou vs. Xu Guocai et al. Objection Case (Main Text): The order of this court to seal up the movables in the Yuxuan Tea Garden at No. 185 Labor Shenfu Road on August 9 of this year shall be revoked. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Wang Zhengyuan et al. vs. Shi Bangjun Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff Wang Zhengyuan 1,000 yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of two percent from August 21, 1930, until the date of final execution. The defendant shall also repay the plaintiff Li Yangshi 300 yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of two percent from the tenth day of the fifth month of 1929 until the date of final execution. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Zhu Tian Shi vs. Zhu Hanqing et al. Separation and Support Case (Main Text): The plaintiff and defendant Zhu Wang Shi are permitted to separate, and defendant Zhu Hanqing shall pay support of 30 yuan per month. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Minfeng Paper Company vs. Huaxin Box Factory et al. Goods Debt Case (Main Text): Defendant Huaxin Box Factory shall repay the plaintiff 760 taels of silver, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from the date of the lawsuit until the date of final execution. If compulsory execution against the property of Huaxin Box Factory is ineffective, defendant Shen Xing shall bear the liability for compensatory damages. The counterclaim of any defendant is dismissed. The litigation costs of both the main lawsuit and the counterclaim shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Shi Shunqing vs. Tang Shifu Rent and Transfer Price Case (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 120 yuan and a transfer price of 180 yuan. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Xinji Bank vs. Ke Beni Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 50 yuan, plus interest at an annual rate of 1.8 percent from November 12, 1931, until the date of final execution, and shall pay interest on the already repaid 200 yuan at the aforementioned interest rate from the date of the loan until the date of repayment. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Lian Fugeng vs. Bian Luo Guanfu Goods Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff a goods debt of 52 yuan, 8 jiao, and 1 fen. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. (Above: October 7)

Shanghai Local Court 298

▲ Criminal Judgment: Judgment on Wang Guankun for Injury and Negligent Homicide Case (Main Text): Wang Guankun is fined 80 yuan for bodily injury and sentenced to three months of imprisonment for negligent homicide, to be served concurrently. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one yuan shall be converted into one day of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment becomes final shall be offset against the imprisonment period at a rate of two days for one day. ▲ Judgment on Yuan Afu for Negligent Homicide Case (Main Text): Yuan Afu is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for professional negligence causing death. The number of days of detention before the judgment becomes final shall be offset against the imprisonment period at a rate of two days for one day. ▲ Judgment on Xu Guibao for Obstructing Family Case (Main Text): Xu Guibao is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for intending to commit adultery and enticing a woman under the age of twenty to leave her guardian. The number of days of detention before the judgment becomes final shall be offset against the imprisonment period at a rate of two days for one day. Xu Guibao shall hand over Jiang A'da to Jiang Yongsen for collection. (Above: October 5)
